### 16.2 Definitions

Definitions of Terms – As used in this Guide are derived from multiple sources, FDA (www.fda.gov), other ISPE
documents (www.ispe.org), ICH (www.ich.org), EFPIA Resource Document (Assessing Facilities Needs for the
Manufacture of Certain Medicinal Products Using a Risk Based Approach, 14 November 2005), EU EudraLex Volume
4 (http://ec.europa.eu/health/documents/eudralex/vol-4/index_en.htm), and various WHO documents (http://www.
who.int/en/).
Acceptable Daily Exposure (ADE)
A dose that is unlikely to cause an adverse effect if an individual is exposed, by any route, at or below this dose
every day for a lifetime. By definition the ADE is intended to be protective of all subpopulations and by all routes
of administration. Establishment of the ADE value is an important first step in a risk assessment and the inherent
assumptions should be consistent with how it is applied within the product mix in a given facility.
Active Pharmaceutical Ingredient (API)
Any substance, or mixture of substances intended to be used in the manufacture of a drug (medicinal) product and
that, when used in the production of a drug, becomes an active ingredient of the drug product. Such substances
are intended to furnish pharmacological activity or other direct effect in the diagnosis, cure, mitigation, treatment, or
prevention of disease, or to affect the structure and function of the body.
Antineoplastic (see Cytostatic and Cytotoxic)
Chemotherapeutic agent that down regulates growth or kills cancer cells. May be classified as cytotoxic or cytostatic.
Aerosol
Suspension of fine solid or liquid particles (e.g., dust, fiber, fog, fume, mist, smoke) in a gas (i.e., typically in air).
Barrier
Facility/room/area, process, equipment, or isolation devices (e.g., glovebox) designed to achieve API or product
containment.
Beta-lactam Antibiotics
Penicillins, cephalosporins, monobactams, and carbapenems, other APIs containing beta-lactam rings, beta-lactamase
inhibitors with beta-lactam rings (e.g., clavulanic acid, and sulbactam and tazobactam).
Bulk
Any product that has completed all processing stages up to, but not including, final packaging.
Campaign
The manufacture of more than one product in a facility, with strict adherence to accepted cleaning procedures
between these products. The products may be run in the same equipment, but not at the same time.

=== PAGE 175 ===
Miss Olga Chung
Taiwan,
Risk-Based Manufacture of Pharmaceutical Products
Appendix 3
Carry Over
The residue or accumulated product on product contact surfaces that is retained after cleaning and may be available
to enter the next product processed with the same product contact surfaces (i.e. it is carried-over to the next product
in production). See definition of Retention.
Clean Zone
An area with defined environmental control of particulate and microbial contamination, constructed and used in such
a way as to reduce the introduction, generation, and retention of contaminants within the area.
Closed Process
A process step (or system) where the product is not exposed to the immediate room environment (and vice versa). It
is the manufacturer’s responsibility to define and prove closure for a process step.
Contained Area
Specific manufacturing space constructed and equipped with appropriate air handling and filtration and operated to
prevent contamination of the external work environment.
Containment
State achieved by enclosures with separation between manufacturing environment and manufacturing operation. The
action of confining a biological agent or other entity within a defined space.
Contaminant
Any particulate, molecular, non-particulate, or biological entity that can adversely affect the product or process.
Contamination
The undesired introduction of impurities of a chemical or microbiological nature, or of foreign matter, into or onto a
raw material, intermediate, or API during production, sampling, packaging or repackaging, storage, or transport.
Controlled Area
Facility space with restricted access and operated to restrict introduction of potential contamination, consequences of
accidental release of airborne contaminants.
Cross-Contamination
Contamination of a starting material, intermediate product or finished product with another starting material or product
during production.
Cytostatic (see Antineoplastic)
Chemotherapeutic agent capable of impairing cell proliferation.
Cytotoxic (see Antineoplastic)
Chemotherapeutic agent intended to control or kill cancer cells, which may act as an indiscriminate poison preventing
cell reproduction or growth and causing death of cancerous and potentially healthy cells.

=== PAGE 176 ===
Miss Olga Chung
Taiwan,
Appendix 3
Risk-Based Manufacture of Pharmaceutical Products
Decontamination
Process that reduces, detoxifies, and/or eliminates contaminated substances to a predetermined acceptance level.
Dedicated Area
Separate area, which may comprise one or more rooms within a multipurpose facility with its own air locked
personnel/material accesses, dedicated to a specific product or product range.
Dedicated Building/Facility
Physically separate or segregated building with its own personnel/material accesses and HVAC systems, dedicated
to process steps associated with a specific product or product.
Dedicated Change Part
An equipment change part (e.g., sieve, filter, etc.) that is dedicated to a specific product or product range, and is
identified accordingly.
Dedicated Equipment
Equipment that is dedicated to a specific product or product range, and is identified accordingly.
Dedicated Suite
One or more rooms within a multipurpose facility or dedicated area that is dedicated to a specific product or product
range, and is identified accordingly.
Detectability
Ability to discover or determine the existence, presence, or fact of a hazard.
Drug (a.k.a., API)
Chemical compound that may be used on, or administered to, humans as an aid in the diagnosis, treatment, cure,
mitigation, or prevention of disease or other abnormal conditions.
Drug Product
A finished dosage form, for example, tablet, capsule, solution, etc., that contains one or more APIs generally, but not
necessarily, in association with inactive ingredients. The term also includes a finished dosage form, which does not
contain an API but it is intended to be used as a placebo.
Excipient (USP)
Components of a finished medicinal drug product other than the API. They are included in the formulation to facilitate
manufacture, enhance stability, control release of API from the product, assist in product identification, or enhance
other product characteristics.
Genotoxic
Substances which damage or modify DNA.

=== PAGE 177 ===
Miss Olga Chung
Taiwan,
Risk-Based Manufacture of Pharmaceutical Products
Appendix 3
GxP Regulation
The underlying international pharmaceutical requirements, such as those set forth in the US FD&C Act, US PHS Act,
FDA regulations, EU Directives, Japanese regulations, or other applicable national legislation or regulations under
which a company operates.
These include, but are not limited to:
•
Good Manufacturing Practice (GMP) (pharmaceutical, including API), veterinary, and blood)
•
Good Clinical Practice (GCP)
•
Good Laboratory Practice (GLP)
•
Good Distribution Practice (GDP)
•
Good Quality Practice (GQP)
•
Good Pharmacovigilance Practice
•
Medical Device Regulations
•
Product Development and Management Association (PDMA) (for regulating free commercial samples)
Hazard
Inherent pharmacologic and toxicologic property of a substance that adversely affects the health of people,
environment, process or product.
Hazardous Substance
A substance which by reason of being explosive, flammable, toxic, poisonous, corrosive, oxidizing, irritant or
otherwise harmful, is likely to cause injury.
Health Hazard
Classification of a chemical for which there is statistically significant scientific data that acute or chronic adverse
health effects may occur in exposed persons. Examples include: cardiovascular toxins, carcinogens, toxic or highly
toxic, developmental, and reproductive toxins, immunotoxic agents, hepatotoxins, nephrotoxins, and neurotoxins.
Highly Hazardous Drugs
Genotoxic compounds that are known to be, or highly likely to be, carcinogenic to humans, compounds that can
produce reproductive and/or developmental effects at low dosages, and compounds that can produce serious target
organ toxicity or other significant adverse effects at low dosages.
Holistic
Considering the whole system or process and its interdependencies rather than addressing separate parts in
isolation.

=== PAGE 178 ===
Miss Olga Chung
Taiwan,
Appendix 3
Risk-Based Manufacture of Pharmaceutical Products
Intermediate
A material produced during steps of the processing of an API that undergoes further molecular change or purification
before it becomes an API. Intermediates may or may not be isolated.
Manufacturing Process
All manufacturing and storage steps in the creation of the finished product from the weighing of components through
the storing, packaging, and labeling of the finished product, including, but not limited to, the following: mixing,
granulating, milling, molding, formulating, lyophilizing, tableting, encapsulating, coating, sterilizing, and filling.
Mix-up
The contamination, at unsafe levels, of one product with another via inadequate plant and process design or human
error.
Multiproduct Facility
A facility that supports production of two or more products, either in a campaigned or concurrent manner.
Mutagenic
Capable of inducing inheritable effect either in vitro and/or in vivo at the genetic (i.e., DNA or chromosomal) level.
No-Observed-Adverse-Effect Level (NOAEL)
The dose in a study which produces no adverse effects.
Occupational Exposure Band (OEB)
A range of airborne concentrations, usually spanning an order of magnitude, corresponding to a category assigned to
a compound based on its inherent toxicological and pharmacological properties. The OEB also corresponds to control
strategies, known in advance, to control airborne levels within the range of concentrations associated with the band.
Occupational Exposure Limit (OEL)
A health-based airborne concentration for a conventional 8-hour workday and a 40-hour workweek, to which it is
believed that nearly all workers may be repeatedly exposed, day after day, for a working lifetime without adverse
effect.
Open System/Process
A system that fails to meet one or more of the requirements that set the criteria for a closed system.
Permitted Daily Exposure (PDE)
A substance specific dose that is unlikely to cause an adverse effect if an individual is exposed at or below this dose
every day for a lifetime.
Pharmaceutical Product
Substance or combination of APIs and excipients, or preservatives which has a therapeutic, prophylactic, or
diagnostic purpose, or is intended to modify physiological functions, and is presented in a dosage form suitable for
administration to the patient.

=== PAGE 179 ===
Miss Olga Chung
Taiwan,
Risk-Based Manufacture of Pharmaceutical Products
Appendix 3
Physical Segregation
The separation of materials, spaces, or operations by means of physical barriers to prevent their mixing or overlap.
Plausible Pathways
A reasonable route of potential exposure.
Point-of-Departure (PoD)
The dose in animals or humans which serves as the starting point for derivation of the ADE value.  This is the dose
associated with the critical effect, which is the most sensitive clinically significant adverse effect observed that is
relevant to humans.
Process Boundary
The process equipment and the interface, through which it is charged, discharged, sampled, intervened, and
recovered.
Product Changeover
The program by which a processing area is cleared of supplies and components used in the manufacture of a
previous product and then readied for production of a new product. This often includes parts change over and/or
special cleaning to eliminate cross-contamination.
Product Life Cycle
All phases in the life of the product from the initial development through marketing until the product’s discontinuation.
Primary Containment
The first level of containment, consisting of the inside portion of that container which comes into immediate contact on
its inner surface with the material being contained.
Quality Risk Management (QRM)
A systematic process for the assessment, control, communication and review of risks to the quality of the drug
product across the product life cycle.
Quality System
The sum of all aspects of a system that implements quality policy and ensures that quality objectives are met.
Retention
The residue, or accumulated product, on product contact surfaces that can carryover from one product to another in
the same equipment used in a sequential or campaign manner.
Risk
Likelihood of an identified harmful consequence as a function of exposure to a hazard.

=== PAGE 180 ===
Miss Olga Chung
Taiwan,
Appendix 3
Risk-Based Manufacture of Pharmaceutical Products
Risk Metrics
A collection of quality, compliance, and/or performance measurements which help management measure and control
the risks associated with operating within a regulated industry.  Also known as dashboards.
Secondary Containment
Level of containment that is external to, and separate from, primary containment.
Self Contained Area
Premises which provide complete and total separation of all aspects of an operation including personnel and
equipment movement, with well established procedures, controls, and monitoring. This includes physical barriers as
well as separate air handling systems, but does not necessarily imply two distinct and separate buildings.
Sensitizer
A compound that can cause immediate (IgE mediated) or delayed (cell-mediated) hypersensitivity reactions.
Segregation
The provision of facilities which, although dedicated to a particular use, can be within the same building as other
operations. A fully segregated area within a common building is one where there is a continuous floor to roof wall (a
floor to ceiling wall, non-segregated roof space is not acceptable). The wall should be sealed at all break points where
common services breach the wall.
Severity
A measure of the seriousness of possible consequences of a hazard.
Teratogenicity
The occurrence of behavioral or structural malformations in a developing foetus when a substance is administered
during pregnancy.
Vaccine
Antigens prepared from modified organisms that elicit immune response (antibody production) to protect a person or
animal from a disease agent.
Wipe Limit
A surface limit applied to external equipment and facility surfaces for the purpose of evaluating worker exposures.
Any use of wipe sample results should be done with caution, within the context of a risk assessment for cross-
contamination based on the underlying ADE value.
